<th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em">Other work</th>
<td>Rocket engineer, NASA, Chief Architect of the Saturn V rocket of the Apollo manned lunar missions, engineering program manager</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Wernher Magnus Maximilian Freiherr von Braun</b> (March 23, 1912 – June 16, 1977) was a German, later American, <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_engineering" title="Aerospace engineering">aerospace engineer</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Space_architecture" title="Space architecture">space architect</a> credited with inventing the <a href="/wiki/V-2_rocket" title="V-2 rocket">V-2 rocket</a> for <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">Saturn V</a> for the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> He was one of the leading figures in the development of rocket technology in Nazi Germany, where he was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a>.</p>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, he was secretly moved to the United States, along with about 1,500 other scientists, engineers, and technicians, as part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Paperclip" title="Operation Paperclip">Operation Paperclip</a>, where he developed the rockets that launched the United States' first space satellite <a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a> manned lunar landings.</p>
<p>In his twenties and early thirties, von Braun worked in Germany's rocket development program, where he helped design and develop the V-2 rocket at <a href="/wiki/Peenem%C3%BCnde" title="Peenemünde">Peenemünde</a> during World War II. Following the war, von Braun worked for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> on an <a href="/wiki/Intermediate-range_ballistic_missile" title="Intermediate-range ballistic missile">intermediate-range ballistic missile</a> (IRBM) program before his group was assimilated into <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>. Under NASA, he served as director of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">Marshall Space Flight Center</a> and as the chief architect of the Saturn V launch vehicle, the superbooster that propelled the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_(spacecraft)" title="Apollo (spacecraft)">Apollo spacecraft</a> to the Moon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAMSFC_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAMSFC-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1975, he received the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>. He continued insisting on the <a href="/wiki/Human_mission_to_Mars" title="Human mission to Mars">human mission to Mars</a> throughout his life.</p>
<p></p>
